   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of states and territories of the United States</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Wikipedia list article
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "States of America" redirects here. For the sovereign states of the Americas, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_the_Americas" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in the Americas">List of sovereign states and dependent territories in the Americas</a>. For the nation sometimes referred to as the United States of America, see <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For a broader coverage related to this topic, see <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">Territories of the United States</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png/330px-Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png/495px-Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png/660px-Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1236"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of the United States showing its 50 <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a>, <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia">federal district</a> and five inhabited <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">territories</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal republic</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> consisting of 50 <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Capital_districts_and_territories#United_States" title="Capital districts and territories">federal district</a> (<a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> of the United States), five major <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">territories</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands" title="United States Minor Outlying Islands">minor islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">48 contiguous states</a> and Washington, D.C., are in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> between <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> is in the far northwestern part of North America and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the mid-<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a>. Territories of the United States are scattered throughout the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. </p>
      <p>States possess a number of powers and rights under the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, such as regulating intrastate commerce, running <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_United_States" title="Elections in the United States">elections</a>, creating <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States" title="Local government in the United States">local governments</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratifying</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_amendment#United_States" title="Constitutional amendment">constitutional amendments</a>. Each state has its own <a href="/wiki/State_constitution_(United_States)" title="State constitution (United States)">constitution</a>, grounded in <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_States" title="Republicanism in the United States">republican principles</a>, and government, consisting of three branches: <a href="/wiki/Governor_(United_States)" title="Governor (United States)">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/State_court_(United_States)" title="State court (United States)">judicial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> All states and their residents are represented in the federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> legislature consisting of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>. Each state is represented by two senators, while representatives are <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_apportionment" title="United States congressional apportionment">distributed</a> among the states in proportion to the most recent <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">constitutionally</a> mandated decennial <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Additionally, each state is entitled to select a number of electors to vote in the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a>, the body that elects the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president of the United States</a>, equal to the total of representatives and senators in Congress from that state.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Article_Four_of_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Article Four of the United States Constitution">Article IV</a>, Section 3, Clause 1 of the Constitution grants to Congress the authority to <a href="/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union" title="Admission to the Union">admit</a> new states into the Union. Since the establishment of the United States in 1776, the number of states has expanded from <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">the original 13</a> to the current total of 50, and each new state is admitted on an <a href="/wiki/Equal_footing" title="Equal footing">equal footing</a> with the existing states.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As provided by <a href="/wiki/Article_One_of_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Article One of the United States Constitution">Article I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enumerated_powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Enumerated powers">Section 8</a> of the Constitution, Congress exercises "exclusive jurisdiction" over the federal district, which is not part of any state. Prior to passage of the 1973 <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_Home_Rule_Act" title="District of Columbia Home Rule Act">District of Columbia Home Rule Act</a>, which devolved certain Congressional powers to an elected <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_the_District_of_Columbia" title="Mayor of the District of Columbia">mayor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_District_of_Columbia" title="Council of the District of Columbia">council</a>, the district did not have an elected local government. Even so, Congress retains the right to review and overturn laws created by the council and intervene in local affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> As it is not a state, the district does not have <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_voting_rights" title="District of Columbia voting rights">representation</a> in the Senate. However, since 1971, its residents have been represented in the House of Representatives by a non-voting <a href="/wiki/Non-voting_members_of_the_United_States_House_of_representatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-voting members of the United States House of representatives">delegate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Additionally, since 1961, following ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-third_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-third Amendment to the United States Constitution">23rd Amendment</a>, the district has been entitled to select three electors to vote in the Electoral College. </p>
      <p>In addition to the 50 states and federal district, the United States has <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over 14 <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">territories</a>. Five of them (<a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>) have a permanent, nonmilitary population, while nine of them do not. With the exception of <a href="/wiki/Navassa_Island" title="Navassa Island">Navassa Island</a>, Puerto Rico, and the U.S. Virgin Islands, which are located in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, all territories are located in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. One territory, <a href="/wiki/Palmyra_Atoll" title="Palmyra Atoll">Palmyra Atoll</a>, is considered to be <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States#Incorporated_and_unincorporated_territories" title="Territories of the United States">incorporated</a>, meaning the full body of the Constitution has been applied to it; the other territories are <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States" title="Unincorporated territories of the United States">unincorporated</a>, meaning the Constitution does not fully apply to them. Ten territories (the Minor Outlying Islands and American Samoa) are considered to be <a href="/wiki/Unorganized_territory#United_States_territory" title="Unorganized territory">unorganized</a>, meaning they have not had an <a href="/wiki/Organic_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Organic Act">Organic Act</a> enacted by Congress; the four other territories are <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">organized</a>, meaning they have had an Organic Act that has been enacted by Congress. The five inhabited territories each have limited autonomy and a non-voting delegate in Congress, in addition to having territorial legislatures and governors, but residents cannot vote in federal elections. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> is the most populous state, with 39,512,223 residents (2020 estimate); <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> is the least populous, with an estimated 582,658 residents. The District of Columbia, with an estimated 646,449 residents as of 2012, has a higher population than the two least populous states (Wyoming and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>). The largest state by area is Alaska, encompassing 665,384 square miles (1,723,340&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>), while the smallest is <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, encompassing 1,545 square miles (4,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). The first state to ratify the current Constitution was <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, which it did on December 7, 1787, while the newest state is Hawaii, which was admitted to the Union on August 21, 1959. The largest territory in terms of both population and size is Puerto Rico, with 3,725,789 residents as of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a> and a total area of 5,325 square miles (13,790&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="States">States</span></h2> 
      <p>The table below lists the 50 <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a>, with their current <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of largest cities of U.S. states and territories by population">largest city</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[A]</a></sup> the date they ratified the U.S. Constitution or were admitted to the Union, population and area data, and number of representative(s) in the U.S. House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[B]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="text-align: center;"> 
       <caption>
        States of the United States of America 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col" colspan="2" rowspan="2">Flag, name and<br><a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_abbreviations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of U.S. state abbreviations">postal abbreviation</a><sup id="cite_ref-USPSabbreviations_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USPSabbreviations-14">[12]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th scope="col" colspan="2">Cities </th> 
         <th scope="col" rowspan="2">Ratification or<br>admission<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[C]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th scope="col" rowspan="2">Population<br><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[D]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AnnualEstUS_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnualEstUS-18">[14]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th scope="col" colspan="2">Total area<sup id="cite_ref-areameasurements_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-areameasurements-19">[15]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th scope="col" colspan="2">Land area<sup id="cite_ref-areameasurements_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-areameasurements-19">[15]</a></sup> </th>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territories">Territories</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:US_insular_areas_C.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/US_insular_areas_C.png/440px-US_insular_areas_C.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/US_insular_areas_C.png/660px-US_insular_areas_C.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/US_insular_areas_C.png/880px-US_insular_areas_C.png 2x" data-file-width="1482" data-file-height="624"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:US_insular_areas_C.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>A map showing the location of each territory controlled by the United States. The United States is marked in blue, inhabited territories are marked in green, and uninhabited territories are marked in orange.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>

         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> </td>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: upper-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The largest city is the city in a state with the largest population in the <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">city proper</a> (as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>).</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Each state is entitled to at least one representative. Current federal law sets the number of voting members of the House of Representatives at 435, which are apportioned among states every ten years according to their relative population.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Each state is also entitled to two senators.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The original 13 states became <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> in July 1776 upon agreeing to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>, and each joined the first Union of states between 1777 and 1781, upon ratifying the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> These states are presented in the order in which each ratified the 1787 Constitution, thus joining the present federal Union of states. Subsequent states are listed in the order of their admission to the Union, and the date given is the official establishment date set by <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Congress" title="Act of Congress">Act of Congress</a>. <i>For further details, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_admission_to_the_Union" title="List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union">List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union</a></i></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2019 estimate</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-statenomenclature-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-statenomenclature_21-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-statenomenclature_21-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-statenomenclature_21-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-statenomenclature_21-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Uses the <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature" title="Nomenclature">term</a> "<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">commonwealth</a>" rather than "state" in its full official name.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2019 estimate</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-nv-d-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-nv-d_25-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nv-d_25-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nv-d_25-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nv-d_25-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nv-d_25-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Represented by a non-voting delegate in the House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Non-voting_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Non-voting-24">[18]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2015 population estimate for: American Samoa, Guam, Northern Mariana Islands, and Virgin Islands; 2019 population estimate for Puerto Rico.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although not organized through a federal organic act or other explicit Congressional directive on governance, the people of American Samoa adopted a constitution in 1967, and then in 1977, elected territorial officials for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-InteriorAS_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InteriorAS-30">[22]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-2organized-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-2organized_35-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2organized_35-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Organized as a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">commonwealth</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-nv-r-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nv-r_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Represented by a non-voting <a href="/wiki/Resident_Commissioner_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Resident Commissioner of Puerto Rico">resident commissioner</a> in the House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Non-voting_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Non-voting-24">[18]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Excluding <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoon</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although there are no indigenous inhabitants, around 40 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a> staff and service contractors live on the island at any given time.<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Pacific_Islands_Wildlife_Refuges_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Pacific_Islands_Wildlife_Refuges-45">[33]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">U.S. <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> is disputed by <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HaitiNavassa_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HaitiNavassa-49">[36]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although there are no indigenous inhabitants, between four and 20 <a href="/wiki/The_Nature_Conservancy" title="The Nature Conservancy">Nature Conservancy</a>, employees, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a> staff, and researchers live on the island at any given time.<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Pacific_Islands_Wildlife_Refuges_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Pacific_Islands_Wildlife_Refuges-45">[33]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although there are no indigenous inhabitants, as of 2009, around 150 U.S. 150 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">U.S. military personnel</a> and civilian contractors were living on the island, staffing the <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island_Airfield" title="Wake Island Airfield">Wake Island Airfield</a> and communications facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Wake_Island_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wake_Island-53">[38]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">U.S. <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> is disputed by the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[39]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is the approximate figure for the land area of the bank, and does not include the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This figure includes the total land area of the Serranilla Bank and the water area of its lagoon, but not the surrounding territorial waters.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
